10-awesome-corporate-blogs-from-the-best-content-marketing-brandswraokuwfwvq,rk,10 Awesome Corporate Blogs from the Best Content Marketing Brands,<div>\n<section><nav></nav>\n<p>Blogging is essential for any company that wants to connect with consumers online.&nbsp;<a href="http://socialmediapearls.com/corporate-blogs/">70% of buyers&nbsp;</a>learn about a company through posts rather than ads. But while it&rsquo;s easy to start a blog\, it&rsquo;s not always easy to publish valuable\, engaging posts on a regular basis.</p>\n</section>\n</div>\n<div id="start">\n<p>The best way to learn? By example.</p>\n<p>The 10 corporate blogs below\, in no particular order\, consistently deliver valuable\, relevant\, engaging content\, while exhibiting a clear business strategy with a high potential for conversion.</p>\n<h2>LinkedIn</h2>\n<p><img style="height: auto;" src="https://uplandsoftware.com/kapost/wp-content/uploads/sites/37/2019/10/linkedin-blog.png" alt="" width="600" height="497"></p>\n<p>From social networking to global publishing\, the successful rollout of LinkedIn&rsquo;s crowdsourced content generation platform piqued the curiosity of the opportunistic blogger in us all. What could have been a potentially cacophonous endeavor has instead enabled 330+ million users to adequately show&nbsp;<em>and</em>&nbsp;tell in a professional setting\, with their professional network\, on an aesthetic interface. The posts are curated by a content aggregation platform\, aptly dubbed&nbsp;<a href="http://www.linkedin.com/today/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">The Pulse</a>\, that makes for a relevant and valuable user-centric experience and fosters engagement.</p>\n<p>The company&rsquo;s&nbsp;<a href="http://blog.linkedin.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">official blog</a>&nbsp;offers consistent industry insights and guidance to job seekers\, recruiters\, employers\, and employees alike. Tips on how to navigate and utilize LinkedIn advantageously\, incumbent career advice\, and industry-specific data are just some examples of what LinkedIn&rsquo;s now burgeoning blogosphere has to offer.</p>\n<h2>Buffer</h2>\n<p><img style="height: auto;" src="https://uplandsoftware.com/kapost/wp-content/uploads/sites/37/2019/10/buffer-blog.png" alt="" width="600" height="329"></p>\n<p>Buffer&rsquo;s simply-designed blog\,&nbsp;<a href="https://blog.bufferapp.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Buffer Social</a>\, is a pleasant call to action to the uninitiated and a valuable\, consistent resource for social media marketers of all levels of experience.</p>\n<p>The blog itself hosts a header\, of sorts\, that informs users of the company&rsquo;s ability to save you time and provides an ad hoc testimonial from a few large companies. Following the digital conversion nudge are the posts themselves\, loaded with pearls of social media wisdom. Not to mention: undoubtedly engaging as each post hosts a significant number of comments and social shares.</p>\n<h2>HubSpot</h2>\n<p><img style="height: auto;" src="https://uplandsoftware.com/kapost/wp-content/uploads/sites/37/2019/10/hubspot-blog.png" alt="" width="600" height="342"></p>\n<p>Pumping out roughly 10 posts on a given day\, HubSpot clearly has a deep understanding of how to provide value to marketers\, salespeople\, and agencies around the world. The inbound marketing mecca resembles their name with an aesthetic\, well-written&nbsp;<a href="http://http//blog.hubspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">blog</a>&nbsp;that has become an industry-wide resource to individuals and to companies of all sizes. It is intelligently organized\, elegantly designed\, and brimming with relevant content.</p>\n<h2>IBM</h2>\n<p><strong><img style="height: auto;" src="https://uplandsoftware.com/kapost/wp-content/uploads/sites/37/2019/10/ibm-blog.png" alt="" width="600" height="307"></strong></p>\n<p>With their&nbsp;<a href="http://www.ibm.com/smarterplanet/us/en/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">A Smarter Planet</a>&nbsp;campaign\, IBM has created a robust nerve center for their content marketing efforts. Peripherally\, they have developed an impressive arsenal of blogs committed to a number of seemingly disparate communities. From&nbsp;<a href="https://www-304.ibm.com/connections/blogs/bcde08b8-816c-42a8-aa37-5f1ce02470a9/?lang=en_us" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">software</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a href="https://www-304.ibm.com/connections/blogs/socialbusiness/?lang=en_us" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">social</a>\,&nbsp;<a href="https://www-304.ibm.com/connections/blogs/aim/?lang=en_us" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">connections</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a href="http://www.ibm.com/cloud-computing/us/en/community.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">cloud</a>\,&nbsp;<a href="http://www.ibmbigdatahub.com/blogs" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">big data</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a href="https://www-304.ibm.com/connections/blogs/businessinsight/?lang=en_us" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">business</a>\, the global tech giant seems to cover an encyclopedic list of topics over a myriad of industries.</p>\n<p>If blogging were a hypothetical dragon\, then IBM would be thy dragon slayer.</p>\n<p>Bravo\, IBM. Bravo.</p>\n<h2>Marketo</h2>\n<p><strong><img style="height: auto;" src="https://uplandsoftware.com/kapost/wp-content/uploads/sites/37/2019/10/marketo-blog.png" alt="" width="600" height="366"></strong></p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>Featuring topics such as&nbsp;<a href="http://blog.marketo.com/2014/12/the-holidays-are-here-the-psychology-of-impulse-buying-infographic.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">infographics on the psychology of impulse buying</a>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<a href="http://blog.marketo.com/2014/12/the-next-era-of-marketing-hear-from-seth-godin.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">interviews with Seth Godin</a>&nbsp;on the future of marketing\, Marketo consistently delivers relevant and engaging information to throngs of content hungry marketers. Marketo is considered to be a leader in the digital marketing software industry\, so it seems only natural to find their blog full of high-quality\, well-organized\, superbly-written\, &uuml;ber-hyphenated gems.</p>\n<h2>Hootsuite</h2>\n<p><img style="height: auto;" src="https://uplandsoftware.com/kapost/wp-content/uploads/sites/37/2019/10/hootsuit-blog.png" alt="" width="600" height="340"></p>\n<p>The social media management company&rsquo;s blog offers an intangible value that is difficult to put into words.</p>\n<p>Accessible. Let&rsquo;s just say it&rsquo;s accessible.</p>\n<p>Although it contains a wealth of information on&nbsp;<a href="http://blog.hootsuite.com/4-parts-of-social-media-that-are-constantly-evolving-and-how-to-adapt/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">the evolving social media horizon</a>&nbsp;and in-depth discussions on engagement techniques\, it offers value to social media newbies and pros alike. It&rsquo;s not overtly technical or narrowly targeted\, and it exhibits a minimalistic\, yet aesthetically appealing design.</p>\n<h2>Etsy</h2>\n<p><img style="height: auto;" src="https://uplandsoftware.com/kapost/wp-content/uploads/sites/37/2019/10/etsy-blog.png" alt="" width="600" height="340"></p>\n<p>The peer-to-peer e-commerce sensation\, Etsy\, offers a whopping 8 unique blogs aimed to attract a global audience. From the&nbsp;<a href="https://blog.etsy.com/en/2014/kitchen-histories-the-gingerbread-house/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">history of the gingerbread house</a>&nbsp;to featured shops\, or the&nbsp;<a href="https://blog.etsy.com/en/category/seller-handbook/?ref=blog" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Seller&rsquo;s Handbook</a>&nbsp;to company news\, Etsy&rsquo;s octo-blog offers a little something for everyone.&nbsp;The posts typically have a high level of engagement\, many with hundreds of comments\, and&nbsp;are consistently accompanied by alluring photographs and artwork; unsurprisingly\, nothing on Etsy lacks in the visual design category.</p>\n<h2>The Creators Project</h2>\n<p><img style="height: auto;" src="https://uplandsoftware.com/kapost/wp-content/uploads/sites/37/2019/10/the_creators_project-blog.png" alt="" width="600" height="275"></p>\n<p>Intel partnered with Vice to create what has now become a focal point for the multinational chip-maker&rsquo;s content marketing strategy\, entitled&nbsp;<a href="https://creators.vice.com/en_us" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">The Creators project</a>. As their mission statement suggests\, this blog features &ldquo;visionary artists across multiple disciplines using technology in innovative ways to push the boundaries of creative expression.&rdquo; Subsequently\, the blog is jam-packed with posts ranging from mind-controlled robotic arms to a retirement community being featured on the latest Modest Mouse album cover. With many daily posts\, the content is fresh\, entertaining\, and engaging to even the artistic philistine.</p>\n<h2>Salesforce</h2>\n</div>,published,\N,public,0,Other,Why optimize your warehouse with a data lakehouse strategy.png,Blogging is essential for any company that wants to connect with consumers online. 70% of buyers learn about a company through posts rather than ads. The wrapper is the actual grid and the items are the content inside the grid.</mark></p>\r\n<p id="6f1e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Here&rsquo;s the markup for a wrapper with six items in it:</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="6bb5" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">&lt;div class="wrapper"&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;1&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;2&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;3&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;4&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;5&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;6&lt;/div&gt;<br>&lt;/div&gt;</span></pre>\r\n<p id="a004" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">To turn our wrapper&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">div</code>&nbsp;into a&nbsp;<strong class="kg ir">grid</strong>\, we simply give it a display of&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid</code>:</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="d84c" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.wrapper {<br>    display: grid;<br>}</span></pre>\r\n<p id="d4c9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">But\, this doesn&rsquo;t do anything yet\, as we haven&rsquo;t defined how we want our grid to look like. It&rsquo;ll simply stacks 6&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">div's</code>&nbsp;on top of each other.</p>\r\n<figure class="jt ju jv jw gh jx fv fw paragraph-image">\r\n<div class="jy jz dj ka bg kb" tabindex="0" role="button">\r\n<div class="fv fw nz"><picture><source srcset="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/format:webp/1*vTY7C5FMIp8OLkjrgp-vBg.png 640w\, loading="lazy"></picture></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<figcaption class="oa dn fx fv fw ob oc be b bf z dl" data-selectable-paragraph="">I&rsquo;ve added a bit of styling\, but that hasn&rsquo;t got anything to do with CSS grid.</figcaption>\r\n</figure>\r\n<h1 id="6acc" class="mk ml iq be mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Columns and rows</h1>\r\n<p id="13a4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ni je kj kk nj jh km kn nk kp kq kr nl kt ku kv nm kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">To make it two-dimensional\, we&rsquo;ll need to define the columns and rows. Let&rsquo;s create three columns and two rows. We&rsquo;ll use the&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid-template-row</code>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid-template-column</code>&nbsp;properties.</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="924d" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.wrapper {<br>    display: grid;<br>    grid-template-columns: 100px 100px 100px;<br>    grid-template-rows: 50px 50px;<br>}</span></pre>\r\n<p id="be1f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">As we&rsquo;ve written three values for&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid-template-columns</code>\, we&rsquo;ll get three columns. We&rsquo;ll get two rows\, as we&rsquo;ve specified two values for the&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid-template-rows</code>.</p>\r\n<p id="70f9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">The values dictate how wide we want our columns to be (100px) and how tall we&rsquo;d want our rows to be (50px). Here&rsquo;s the result:</p>\r\n<figure class="jt ju jv jw gh jx fv fw paragraph-image">\r\n<div class="jy jz dj ka bg kb" tabindex="0" role="button">\r\n<div class="fv fw od"><picture><source When we made the first item take up the entire first row\, it pushed the rest of the items down.</p>\r\n<p id="81bd" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Finally\, I&rsquo;d like to show a simpler way of writing the syntax above:</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="e06a" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.item1 {<br>    grid-column: 1 / 4;<br>}</span></pre>\r\n<p id="04c5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">To make sure you&rsquo;ve understood this concept properly\, let&rsquo;s rearrange the items a little bit.</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="d9d2" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.item1 {<br>    grid-column-start: 1;<br>    grid-column-end: 3;<br>}</span><span id="aaf4" class="nr ml iq no b gm on nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.item3 {<br>    grid-row-start: 2;<br>    grid-row-end: 4;<br>}</span><span id="ad3e" class="nr ml iq no b gm on nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.item4 {<br>    grid-column-start: 2;<br>    grid-column-end: 4;<br>}</span></pre>\r\n<p id="31b9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Here&rsquo;s how that looks on the page. Try to wrap you head around why it looks like it does. It shouldn&rsquo;t be too hard.</p>\r\n<figure class="jt ju jv jw gh jx fv fw paragraph-image">\r\n<div class="jy jz dj ka bg kb" tabindex="0" role="button">\r\n<div class="fv fw oo"><picture><source Merry Christmas!</h2>\r\n<div class="mc l">\r\n<h3 class="be b gm z fd ma ff fg mb fi fk dl">13 interactive screencasts to take you from beginner to advanced.</h3>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class="md l">\r\n<p class="be b dm z fd ma ff fg mb fi fk dl">medium.freecodecamp.org</p>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class="me l">\r\n<div class="mf l mg mh mi me mj kc lv">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</a></div>\r\n<p id="96df" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now let&rsquo;s jump into it!</p>\r\n<h1 id="ddbc" class="mk ml iq be mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Your first grid layout</h1>\r\n<p id="f256" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ni je kj kk nj jh km kn nk kp kq kr nl kt ku kv nm kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph=""><mark class="uh ui ao">The two core ingredients of a CSS Grid are the&nbsp;</mark><mark class="uh ui ao"><strong class="kg ir">wrapper&nbsp;</strong></mark><mark class="uh ui ao">(parent)</mark><mark class="uh ui ao"><strong class="kg ir">&nbsp;</strong></mark><mark class="uh ui ao">and the&nbsp;</mark><mark class="uh ui ao"><strong class="kg ir">items&nbsp;</strong></mark><mark class="uh ui ao">(children). The wrapper is the actual grid and the items are the content inside the grid.</mark></p>\r\n<p id="6f1e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Here&rsquo;s the markup for a wrapper with six items in it:</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="6bb5" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">&lt;div class="wrapper"&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;1&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;2&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;3&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;4&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;5&lt;/div&gt;<br>  &lt;div&gt;6&lt;/div&gt;<br>&lt;/div&gt;</span></pre>\r\n<p id="a004" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">To turn our wrapper&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">div</code>&nbsp;into a&nbsp;<strong class="kg ir">grid</strong>\, we simply give it a display of&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid</code>:</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="d84c" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.wrapper {<br>    display: grid;<br>}</span></pre>\r\n<p id="d4c9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">But\, this doesn&rsquo;t do anything yet\, as we haven&rsquo;t defined how we want our grid to look like. It&rsquo;ll simply stacks 6&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">div's</code>&nbsp;on top of each other.</p>\r\n<figure class="jt ju jv jw gh jx fv fw paragraph-image">\r\n<div class="jy jz dj ka bg kb" tabindex="0" role="button">\r\n<div class="fv fw nz"><picture><source srcset="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/format:webp/1*vTY7C5FMIp8OLkjrgp-vBg.png 640w\, loading="lazy"></picture></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<figcaption class="oa dn fx fv fw ob oc be b bf z dl" data-selectable-paragraph="">I&rsquo;ve added a bit of styling\, but that hasn&rsquo;t got anything to do with CSS grid.</figcaption>\r\n</figure>\r\n<h1 id="6acc" class="mk ml iq be mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Columns and rows</h1>\r\n<p id="13a4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ni je kj kk nj jh km kn nk kp kq kr nl kt ku kv nm kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">To make it two-dimensional\, we&rsquo;ll need to define the columns and rows. Let&rsquo;s create three columns and two rows. We&rsquo;ll use the&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid-template-row</code>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid-template-column</code>&nbsp;properties.</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="924d" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.wrapper {<br>    display: grid;<br>    grid-template-columns: 100px 100px 100px;<br>    grid-template-rows: 50px 50px;<br>}</span></pre>\r\n<p id="be1f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">As we&rsquo;ve written three values for&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid-template-columns</code>\, we&rsquo;ll get three columns. We&rsquo;ll get two rows\, as we&rsquo;ve specified two values for the&nbsp;<code class="es nw nx ny no b">grid-template-rows</code>.</p>\r\n<p id="70f9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">The values dictate how wide we want our columns to be (100px) and how tall we&rsquo;d want our rows to be (50px). Here&rsquo;s the result:</p>\r\n<figure class="jt ju jv jw gh jx fv fw paragraph-image">\r\n<div class="jy jz dj ka bg kb" tabindex="0" role="button">\r\n<div class="fv fw od"><picture><source srcset="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/format:webp/1*fJNIdDiScjhI9CZjdxv3Eg.png 640w\, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:720/format:webp/1*fJNIdDiScjhI9CZjdxv3Eg.png 720w\, When we made the first item take up the entire first row\, it pushed the rest of the items down.</p>\r\n<p id="81bd" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Finally\, I&rsquo;d like to show a simpler way of writing the syntax above:</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="e06a" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.item1 {<br>    grid-column: 1 / 4;<br>}</span></pre>\r\n<p id="04c5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">To make sure you&rsquo;ve understood this concept properly\, let&rsquo;s rearrange the items a little bit.</p>\r\n<pre class="jt ju jv jw gh nn no np nq ax gv bj"><span id="d9d2" class="nr ml iq no b gm ns nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.item1 {<br>    grid-column-start: 1;<br>    grid-column-end: 3;<br>}</span><span id="aaf4" class="nr ml iq no b gm on nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.item3 {<br>    grid-row-start: 2;<br>    grid-row-end: 4;<br>}</span><span id="ad3e" class="nr ml iq no b gm on nt l nu nv" data-selectable-paragraph="">.item4 {<br>    grid-column-start: 2;<br>    grid-column-end: 4;<br>}</span></pre>\r\n<p id="31b9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ke kf iq kg b kh ki je kj kk kl jh km kn ko kp kq kr ks kt ku kv kw kx ky kz ij bj" data-selectable-paragraph="">Here&rsquo;s how that looks on the page. Try to wrap you head around why it looks like it does. It shouldn&rsquo;t be too hard.</p>\r\n<figure class="jt ju jv jw gh jx fv fw paragraph-image">\r\n<div class="jy jz dj ka bg kb" tabindex="0" role="button">\r\n<div class="fv fw oo"><picture><source 12-websites-you'll-love-as-a-developerkp3lft6of6,rk,12 Websites You’ll Love As A Developer,<p>Websites are now an essential tool for every business. And if you are a web developer and need to find new material or resources\, then this is the place for you. As a developer\, it is not easy to find a website that can provide all the resources and information that you need. This article will take you through 12 websites that you&rsquo;ll love as a developer.</p>\n<p>Ray.so<br>Turn your code into beautiful images using this site. You can choose from a range of syntax colors\, hide or show the background\, and toggle between a dark and light window. If you are a developer you can easily create beautiful screenshots of source code through this app and share on various social apps such as instagram\, twitter and facebook.</p>\n<p><br>ray.so</p>\n<p>Roadmap.sh<br>Roadmap.sh is a community effort to create roadmaps\, guides and other educational content to help guide the developers in picking up the path and guide their learnings. It contains community curated roadmaps\, study plans\, paths and resources for developers newly entered into this space. It started as a set of charts to guide the developers who are confused about what should learn next.</p>\n<p><br>roadmap.sh</p>\n<p>Codepen.io<br>CodePen is a social development environment. It allows you to write code in the browser\, and see the results of it as you build. You can build and deploy websites\, show off your work\, build test cases to learn and debug\, and find inspiration. You can also browse and share work from other designers and developers in the front-end community.</p>\n<p>Codepen Pro having Pair Program feature where you can use Collab Mode which allows more than one person to edit a Pen at the same time. This is real-time pair programming at its best\, since the two (or more) people can be anywhere in the world and it&rsquo;s not nearly as bandwidth-intensive as video.</p>\n<p><br>codepen.io</p>\n<p>Stack Overflow<br>It is the most common website all most all developers using in everyday work. Stack Overflow is a question-and-answer site for computer programming questions\, especially those related to specific programming languages. It also offers professional development opportunities to its members through online courses\, certificates\, and job listings. Stack Overflow is a public Q&amp;A platform that over 100 million people visit every month to ask questions\, learn\, and share technical knowledge.</p>\n<p><br>stackoverflow.com</p>\n<p>Github<br>GitHub is a website that hosts Git repositories and provides social networking-like features for programmers to share their projects. Github is the complete developer platform to build\, scale\, and deliver secure software.</p>\n<p>GitHub is where over 94 million developers shape the future of software\, together. It Supercharge your development process. Github provides unlimited repositories\, best-in-class version control\, and the world&rsquo;s most powerful open source community-so your team can work more efficiently together.</p>\n<p><br>github.com</p>\n<p>Iconstore.co<br>IconStore is a library of free\, vector (SVG) icons created by talented designers to download for commercial use.</p>\n<p>All the icons published on the IconStore are made to be used freely.</p>\n<p>🟢 Permissions:</p>\n<p>✔ You can use the icons in personal and commercial projects<br>✔ You can modify the icons<br>✔ No attribution required (although it&rsquo;s appreciated!)</p>\n<p>iconstore.co</p>\n<p>Readme.so<br>Use markdown editor and templates to easily create a ReadMe for your next projects. Easy way to create a README file using simple editor provided by the application. It allows you to quickly add and customize all the sections you need for your project&rsquo;s readme.</p>\n<p><br>readme.so</p>\n<p>Lorem Picsum<br>Lorem Picsum provides random or specific uploaded images as placeholders. Here you can view all the images Lorem Picsum provides. Developers need to specify a desired image size (width &amp; height) at the end of the request URL.</p>\n<p><br>picsum.photos</p>\n<p>GitBook<br>GitBook is a modern documentation platform where teams can document everything from products to internal knowledge bases and APIs. It makes it easy to research\, plan and document products\, from start to ship.</p>\n<p><br>gitbook.com</p>\n<p>Figma<br>Figmais a collaborative web application for interface design\, with additional offline features enabled by desktop applications for macOS and Windows. Build an iterative design flow with live collaboration that keeps you in the loop whether you&rsquo;re working in the office or remotely. This has enabled our product teams to ship new products faster and feel more confident in their decisions.</p>\n<p><br>figma.com</p>\n<p>LottieFiles<br>Lottie is a JSON-based animation file format that enables designers to ship animations on any platform as easily as shipping static assets. They are small files that work on any device and can scale up or down without pixelation. LottieFiles lets you create\, edit\, test\, collaborate and ship a Lottie in the easiest way possible. LottieFiles takes away the complexity from Motion Design.</p>\n<p><br>lottiefiles.com</p>\n<p>Dribbble<br>Millions of designers and agencies around the world showcase their portfolio work on Dribbble. Dribbbleis the world&rsquo;s leading destination for designers to learn\, share\, grow\, and get hired. Dribbble market place brings you creative projects to life starting from fonts\, graphics\, themes\, photos\, and templates designed\, mockups and 3D models created by independent creators around the world.</p>\n<p><br>dribbble.com</p>\n<p>There you have it. Thanks for checking this out and do not forget to try these tools.</p>,published,\N,public,0,Developer,12 Websites You’ll Love As A Developer.png,\nWebsites are now an essential tool for every business. data-selectable-paragraph="">Developing a notification layer is a common task when designing a new application. It typically starts with sending a simple email\, but you may manage hundreds of notifications across multiple channels as the application grows. This can be a time-consuming and complex process. That&rsquo;s where Novu comes in. Novu is an infrastructure development platform that helps developers build and deploy cloud-native applications. Its goal is to make it easier for developers to create meaningful\, transactional communication between their product and its users.</p>\n<p id="a531" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Pros</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="750c" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Easy to set up and integrate</li>\n<li id="daab" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Single API for all messaging providers (Email\, SMS\, Push\, Chat)</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="2991" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Cons</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="5551" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">No ORM-based configuration</li>\n<li id="53b1" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">No pricing plans on cloud-managed service</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="5a43" data-selectable-paragraph="">Novu offers an easy-to-use API and a focus on developer experience. This means that developers can easily integrate notifications into their applications without worrying about the underlying infrastructure.</p>\n<p id="574c" data-selectable-paragraph="">With Novu\, you can\,</p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="1a07" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Connect different Providers:</strong>&nbsp;Use a built-in collection of popular providers &mdash; Sendgrid\, Mailgun\, Twilio\, and many more. Add the API key\, and you&rsquo;re ready to go.</li>\n<li id="d0a8" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Set Multiple Notification Channels</strong>: Novu supports many notifications\, including email\, SMS\, push notifications\, and more. This means you can reach your users through their preferred channels and ensure that your messages are delivered.</li>\n<li id="6879" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Use Dynamic Templates</strong>: Select channels\, add content with {{dynamic}} syntax\, and custom rules to control the delivery of notifications.</li>\n<li id="b3d6" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Track Feed</strong>: Novu provides a notification activity feed that monitors every outgoing message associated with its relevant metadata.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="2d0e" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Closed source alternative</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="4e13" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><a href="https://www.courier.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener ugc nofollow">Courier</a></li>\n<li id="be61" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><a href="https://www.magicbell.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener ugc nofollow">Magicbell</a></li>\n</ul>\n<h1 id="a7a3" data-selectable-paragraph="">Appsmith</h1>\n<p id="e3f0" data-selectable-paragraph=""><a href="https://www.appsmith.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener ugc nofollow"><em>https://www.appsmith.com/</em></a></p>\n<blockquote>\n<p id="7a77" data-selectable-paragraph="">📢 In Appsmith&rsquo;s words\, &ldquo;Low code project to build admin panels\, internal tools\, and dashboards. These include popular options like Postgres\, MongoDB\, and Airtable\, as well as the ability to connect to almost every API using the RESTful API or GraphQL plugin.</li>\n<li id="5de2" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>JavaScript code support</strong>. You can use JavaScript inside&nbsp;<code>{{ }}</code>&nbsp;anywhere in Appsmith. id="b114" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">~44K GitHub ⭐</li>\n<li id="6dcf" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Values for community contributions: 4/5</li>\n<li id="8836" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Values for new feature development: 4/5</li>\n<li id="df09" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Speed of Release: 5/5</li>\n<li id="6868" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Support cadence: 4/5</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="7ad7" data-selectable-paragraph="">In recent times\, the competition between databases has evolved. After three decades of growth and improvement\, Postgres has gained a reputation for dependability and high performance\, making it a popular choice among businesses of all sizes. Oracle has compromised the open-source nature of MySQL\, and with the increasing popularity of cloud storage\, Postgres has become a leading open-source database option. The rise of Supabase\, a Postgres-based alternative to Google&rsquo;s Firebase\, reflects the trend of open-source options challenging proprietary ones.</p>\n<p id="b6ab" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Pros</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="9703" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Full Postgres database with Instant REST</li>\n<li id="c9ae" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">It comes with email/social authentication</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="54b7" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Cons</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="1190" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Its SDK only works with JS (Support for other languages is still in beta)</li>\n<li id="c14a" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Security policies are limited in Real-time</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="84cd" data-selectable-paragraph="">With Supabase\, you can\,</p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="da3c" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Set</strong>&nbsp;<strong>Database</strong>: The heart of most applications is storing data and providing users with fast\, easy access. To achieve this\, Supabase relies on PostgreSQL\, an open-source\, relational database. This tech enables Supabase to deliver a seamless experience storing\, retrieving\, and managing data within your applications.</li>\n<li id="c252" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Configure</strong>&nbsp;<strong>Auth:</strong>&nbsp;Supabase makes integrating all major social apps easy\, giving you various options for authenticating your application&rsquo;s users. But if you prefer a more traditional approach\, Supabase also supports email-password authentication.</li>\n<li id="2c09" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Write</strong>&nbsp;<strong>Edge Functions</strong>: Sometimes\, you need to perform certain tasks asynchronously or run operations on the backend of your application. Supabase offers edge functions to handle these types of use cases. Deploying edge functions is easy\, and Supabase distributes them globally to ensure that all users have a consistent\, fast experience.</li>\n<li id="8dbb" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Set-up</strong>&nbsp;<strong>Storage</strong>: As an administrator\, the Supabase platform allows you to manage files from your browser easily. You can search\, upload\, view\, and delete files with a few clicks. Supabase storage integrates seamlessly with PostgreSQL and provides a simple JavaScript API for you to use.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="515e" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Closed source alternative</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="a66c" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><a href="https://firebase.google.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener ugc nofollow">Firebase</a></li>\n</ul>\n<h1 id="a0c2" data-selectable-paragraph="">Supertokens</h1>\n<p id="5eba" data-selectable-paragraph=""><a href="https://supertokens.io/" authentication platform that provides secure and scalable solutions for managing user authentication and authorization in web and mobile applications. One of the main benefits of using a library like supertokens for authentication is that it can save developers significant time and effort. Instead of writing the entire authentication system from scratch\, developers can use the pre-existing and thoroughly tested code provided by supertokens. This can reduce the potential for errors and security vulnerabilities in the authentication process. Additionally\, the open-source nature of supertokens means that developers have access to the source code\, which allows them to customize and extend the library as needed to fit the specific needs of their project.</p>\n<p id="f700" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Pros</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="6a9f" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Modular architecture makes the setup simple.</li>\n<li id="7804" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">It provides an override feature that enables you to customize authentication fully and flows on both your front end and back end.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="53be" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Cons</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="4d23" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">No not support many popular languages like&nbsp;<code>Java</code>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<code>Php</code>\, and they do not have pre-built UI for popular frontend frameworks like&nbsp;<code>Angular</code>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<code>Vue</code>.</li>\n<li id="02a4" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Lacks enterprise features like SCIM provisioning\, admin\, and organization support.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="b0cd" data-selectable-paragraph="">In addition to its core authentication features\, SuperTokens also offers a comprehensive\, end-to-end solution for managing user sessions. With this solution\, it&rsquo;s easy to implement advanced features like synchronizing session data across multiple devices or limiting the number of devices a user can log in to. data-selectable-paragraph="">~24K GitHub ⭐</li>\n<li id="2203" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Values for community contributions: 4/5</li>\n<li id="df77" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Values for new feature development: 4/5</li>\n<li id="0b22" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Speed of Release: 3/5</li>\n<li id="39a9" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Support cadence: 4/5</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="5a37" data-selectable-paragraph="">Astro is a new framework for building websites that allows you to use a JavaScript framework that outputs zero-JavaScript static site. By default\, Astro delivers no JavaScript to the client and renders components into HTML. This helps to speed up the website&rsquo;s performance\, as more JavaScript can lead to slower loading times. If you do need to use JavaScript on your website\, Astro offers the option to use partial hydration through client directives. These directives allow you to specify when and how a component should be hydrated or have JavaScript added to it.</p>\n<p id="daf7" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Pros</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="d382" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Pattern provides all of the benefits of component-based architecture\, such as reusability and maintainability.</li>\n<li id="88da" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Websites are SEO-friendly because all static content is rendered on the server.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="969f" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Cons</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="bc63" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">There is not a lot of debate on the subject (Astro&rsquo;s Island architecture).</li>\n<li id="3fa5" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">A lot of frameworks claim to support the pattern\, which makes it difficult to choose between them.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="ae9f" data-selectable-paragraph="">One of the great things about Astro is that it supports popular component libraries like React/Preact (JSX)\, Svelte\, Vue\, and web components\, making it easy for developers who are already familiar with these tools to get up and running quickly.</p>\n<p id="2799" data-selectable-paragraph="">Astro pitches itself as\,</p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="034b" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Content-focused</strong>: Astro was designed for building content-rich websites. This includes most marketing sites\, publishing sites\, documentation sites\, blogs\, portfolios\, and some eCommerce sites.</li>\n<li id="6c6d" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Server-first</strong>: Astro leverages server-side rendering over client-side rendering as much as possible. This is the same approach traditional server-side frameworks &mdash; PHP\, Ruby on Rails\, etc. &mdash; have been using for decades. But you don&rsquo;t need to learn a second server-side language to unlock it.</li>\n<li id="5047" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Fully flexible</strong>: Astro is an all-in-one web framework with everything you need to build a website. Astro includes a component syntax\, file-based routing\, asset handling\, a build process\, bundling\, optimizations\, data fetching\, and more.</li>\n</ul>\n<h1 id="2084" data-selectable-paragraph="">Nhost</h1>\n<p id="9a11" data-selectable-paragraph=""><a href="https://nhost.io/" target="_blank" rel="noopener ugc data-selectable-paragraph="">In recent years\, GraphQL has gained significant hype as an alternative to REST APIs. GraphQL is a query language that allows clients to request specifically shaped data from a server\, leading to more efficient and flexible communication between client and server.</p>\n<p id="a78e" data-selectable-paragraph="">Nhost is a cloud-based backend platform that utilizes GraphQL to enable developers to build and deploy serverless applications faster. Nhost provides a range of features that make it easy to build scalable and feature-rich applications\, including user management\, data storage\, serverless functions\, real-time communication\, and more.</p>\n<p id="25b6" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Pros</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="52a9" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Provides instant Realtime GraphQL API based on your tables and columns in the database.</li>\n<li id="20bd" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Supports serverless functions.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="0cc4" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Cons</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="71b0" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Real-time options are limited.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="1f19" data-selectable-paragraph="">One of the key benefits of using Nhost is that it allows developers to take advantage of GraphQL without worrying about the complexities of setting up and maintaining their own GraphQL server.</p>\n<p id="a03a" data-selectable-paragraph="">With Nhost\, you can set up\,</p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="8af5" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Auth</strong>: Nhost provides a complete user management system that easily adds authentication and authorization to your application. This includes support for popular authentication methods such as email/password\, social login\, and more.</li>\n<li id="38f3" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Serverless Functions</strong>: Nhost enables you to create custom backend logic and integrations without the need to maintain servers. This makes it easy to add custom functionality to your application and scale it as needed.</li>\n<li id="ccd6" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Real-Time GraphQL API</strong>: Nhost includes a real-time communication engine that allows you to manage subscriptions to sync data in real-time.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="4ae8" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Closed source alternative</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="cbea" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><a href="https://firebase.google.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener ugc nofollow">Firebase</a></li>\n</ul>\n<h1 id="925e" data-selectable-paragraph="">Hoppscotch</h1>\n<p id="15f0" data-selectable-paragraph=""><a href="https://hoppscotch.io/" target="_blank" rel="noopener ugc nofollow"><em>https://hoppscotch.io/</em></a></p>\n<blockquote>\n<p id="4ab6" data-selectable-paragraph="">📢 In Hoppscotch own words\, &ldquo;Hoppscotch is light-weight\, web based API development suite. tool that helps developers test and debugs their APIs quickly and easily. It is a lightweight tool that can be used to send HTTP requests and analyze the responses from the API.</p>\n<p id="6af3" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Pros</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="16a6" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Lightweight and fast.</li>\n<li id="b075" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Documentation generator.</li>\n<li id="70c8" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Support for WebSocket also allows SSE\,&nbsp;<a href="http://socket.io/" target="_blank" rel="noopener ugc nofollow">Socket.IO</a>&nbsp;and MQTT</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="f6ab" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Cons</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="35a1" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Little documentation</li>\n<li id="e6fd" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Missing features for test automation</li>\n<li id="433f" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Need to add some features by CLI.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="2183" data-selectable-paragraph="">One of the critical features of Hoppscotch is its simplicity. It has a straightforward and intuitive interface that makes it easy for developers to get started with API testing. It also includes various features that make it easy to customize and automate API tests\, including support for variables\, environment management\, and more.</p>\n<p id="ea1c" data-selectable-paragraph="">Hopscotch comes with\,</p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="8fad" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>REST and GraphQL Support</strong>: Hoppscotch supports both REST and GraphQL APIs\, making it a versatile tool that can be used to test APIs built using a wide range of technologies.</li>\n<li id="f575" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Realtime Platform</strong>: Hoppscotch includes a real-time platform that allows developers to test and debug their socket or channel connections. This makes it easy to identify and fix issues as they arise.</li>\n<li id="ca3d" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>API Documentation</strong>: Hoppscotch allows developers to create comprehensive API documentation quickly and easily. This can be especially useful for helping other developers understand and use your API.</li>\n<li id="53dd" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>PWA Support</strong>: It is designed to be easy and flexible\, allowing users to create custom databases and workflows to meet their specific needs.</p>\n<p id="fd0b" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Pros</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="9555" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Assign and track tasks\, third-party integration available</li>\n<li id="c748" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Turn your SQL database into a smart spreadsheet</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="39e0" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Cons</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="6f59" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">No cloud version (open in private beta)</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="4367" data-selectable-paragraph="">One of the key features of NocoDB is its customizable data model. management system (CMS) that allows developers to build and manage APIs for content-rich applications. It is designed to be easy and flexible\, allowing developers to quickly build and deploy APIs for their applications.</p>\n<p id="7340" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Pros</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="4bdd" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Rapid and scalable</li>\n<li id="0ee7" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Built-In authentication system</li>\n<li id="a5fd" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Multiple workflows for automations</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="6ff9" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Cons</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="4b39" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">Difficult to migrate existing APIs</li>\n<li id="7ca8" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph="">TypeScript support Is limited</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="df9f" data-selectable-paragraph="">One of the key features of Strapi is its plugin-based architecture. Strapi includes a range of plugins that allow developers to easily add functionality to their APIs\, such as support for file uploads\, email sending\, and more. These plugins can be easily installed and configured\, making it easy to customize the functionality of your API.</p>\n<p id="2188" data-selectable-paragraph="">In addition to its plugin architecture\, Strapi also includes a user-friendly admin panel that allows developers and content editors to manage their content easily. This includes support for creating and managing content types and previewing and publishing content.</p>\n<p id="15d1" data-selectable-paragraph="">With Strapi\, you get\,</p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="e83d" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>GraphQL or RESTful</strong>: Strapi allows developers to choose using GraphQL or RESTful APIs\, depending on their needs. This makes it a flexible platform that can be used to build APIs for various applications.</li>\n<li id="8b8d" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Webhooks</strong>: Strapi includes webhooks support\, allowing developers to trigger custom events and actions based on certain conditions. This can be especially useful for building integrations and automating workflows.</li>\n<li id="bdfb" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Authentication &amp; Permissions</strong>: Strapi includes a user management system that allows developers to easily add authentication and authorization to their APIs. This includes support for popular authentication methods such as email/password\, social login\, and more.</li>\n<li id="bb2a" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Internationalization</strong>: Strapi includes support for internationalization\, which allows developers to build APIs that support multiple languages easily. This can be especially useful for building applications that cater to a global audience.</li>\n</ul>\n<p id="76ab" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong>Closed source alternative</strong></p>\n<ul style="list-style-type: none;">\n<li id="ec5b" style="list-style-type: disc;" data-selectable-paragraph=""><a href="https://www.contentful.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener ugc nofollow">Contentful</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p id="f99b" data-selectable-paragraph="">Thanks for reading this one! why-optimize-your-warehouse-with-a-data-lakehouse-strategyy6w83colew,rk,Why optimize your warehouse with a data lakehouse strategy,<h2>Value of data warehouse optimization</h2>\n<p>Since its introduction over a century ago\, the gasoline-powered engine has remained largely unchanged. It&rsquo;s simply been adapted over time to accommodate modern demands such as pollution controls\, air conditioning and power steering.</p>\n<p>Similarly\, the relational database has been the foundation for data warehousing for as long as data warehousing has been around. Relational databases were adapted to accommodate the demands of new workloads\, such as the data engineering tasks associated with structured and semi-structured data\, and for building machine learning models.</p>\n<p>Returning to the analogy\, there have been significant changes to how we power cars. We now have gasoline-powered engines\, battery electric vehicles (BEVs)\, and hybrid vehicles. An&nbsp;<a href="https://www.forbes.com/sites/brookecrothers/2021/08/15/study-confirms-this-upside-for-tesla-evs-over-gas-cars/?sh=649348696048" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">August 2021 Forbes article</a>&nbsp;referenced a 2021 Department of Energy Argonne National Laboratory publication indicating\, &ldquo;Hybrid electric vehicles (think: Prius) had the lowest total 15-year per-mile cost of driving in the Small SUV category beating BEVs&rdquo;.</p>\n<p>Just as hybrid vehicles help their owners balance the initial purchase price and cost over time\, enterprises are attempting to find a balance between high performance and cost-effectiveness for their data and analytics ecosystem. Essentially\, they want to run the right workloads in the right environment without having to copy datasets excessively.</p>\n<p><img src="https://www.ibm.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2023/04/sylvensteinbridge_dji_0300.l-e1682347613136-630x330.jpg" alt="Aerial view of Sylvenstein Bridge\, Sylvenstein Lake\, Upper Bavaria\, Germany"></p>\n<h2>Optimizing your data lakehouse architecture</h2>\n<p>Fortunately\, the IT landscape is changing thanks to a mix of cloud platforms\, open source and traditional software vendors. The rise of cloud object storage has driven the cost of data storage down. Open-data file formats have evolved to support data sharing across multiple data engines\, like Presto\, Spark and others. Intelligent data caching is improving the performance of data lakehouse infrastructures.</p>\n<p>All these innovations are being adapted by software vendors and accepted by their customers. So\, what does this mean from a practical perspective? What can enterprises do different from what they are already doing today? Some use case examples will help. To effectively use raw data\, it often needs to be curated within a data warehouse. Semi-structured data needs to be reformatted and transformed to be loaded into tables. And ML processes consume an abundance of capacity to build models.</p>\n<p>Organizations running these workloads in their data warehouse environment today are paying a high run rate for engineering tasks that add no additional value or insight. Only the outputs from these data-driven models allow an organization to derive additional value. If organizations could execute these engineering tasks at a lower run rate in a&nbsp;<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Enu-EH7RHHM" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">data lakehouse</a>&nbsp;while making the transformed data available to both the lakehouse and warehouse via open formats\, they could deliver the same output value with low-cost processing.</p>\n<h2>Benefits of optimizing across your data warehouse and data lakehouse</h2>\n<p>Optimizing workloads across a data warehouse and a data lakehouse by sharing data using open formats can reduce costs and complexity. This helps organizations drive a better return on their data strategy and analytics investments while also helping to deliver better data governance and security.</p>\n<p>And just as a hybrid car allows car owners to get greater value from their car investment\, optimizing workloads across a data warehouse and data lakehouse will allow organizations to get greater value from their data analytics ecosystem.</p>\n<p>Discover how you can optimize your data warehouse to scale analytics and artificial intelligence (AI) workloads with a data lakehouse strategy.</p>,published,\N,public,0,Travel,Why optimize your warehouse with a data lakehouse strategy.png,In a prior blog\, we pointed out that warehouses\, known for high-performance data processing for business intelligence\, can quickly become expensive for new data and evolving workloads. We also made the case that query and reporting\, provided by big data engines such as Presto\, need to work with the Spark infrastructure framework to support advanced analytics and complex enterprise data decision-making. To do so\, Presto and Spark need to readily work with existing and modern data warehouse infrastructures. Now\, let’s chat about why data warehouse optimization is a key value of a data lakehouse strategy.
